<p>The <b>2010 <a href="/wiki/FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup" title="FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup">FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup</a></b> <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_association_football" title="Women's association football">women's football</a> tournament is the second such tournament, and was held in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> from September 5–25, 2010. Sixteen teams, comprising representatives from all six confederations, took part in the final competition, in which Trinidad and Tobago had a guaranteed place as the host nation.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Qualified_teams">Qualified teams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Qualified teams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The qualifiers took place during late 2009 and early 2010. The places were allocated as follows to confederations: <a href="/wiki/Asian_Football_Confederation" title="Asian Football Confederation">AFC</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/Confederation_of_African_Football" title="Confederation of African Football">CAF</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/CONCACAF" title="CONCACAF">CONCACAF</a> (2), <a href="/wiki/CONMEBOL" title="CONMEBOL">CONMEBOL</a> (3), <a href="/wiki/Oceania_Football_Confederation" title="Oceania Football Confederation">OFC</a> (1), <a href="/wiki/UEFA" title="UEFA">UEFA</a> (3), plus the host country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></li>
</ul>

<p>On 30 June 2010, President of Nigeria <a href="/wiki/Goodluck_Jonathan" title="Goodluck Jonathan">Goodluck Jonathan</a> announced he would suspend the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_Football_Federation" title="Nigeria Football Federation">Nigeria Football Federation</a> from FIFA competition for 2 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> This put the <a href="/wiki/Nigeria_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Nigeria women's national football team">Flamingoes</a> place at the competition in jeopardy. On 5 July 2010, the ban was lifted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Squads">Squads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Squads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup_squads" title="2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup squads">2010 FIFA U-17 Women's World Cup squads</a></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Venues">Venues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Venues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During preparation four stadia were constructed in 2001. These four venues along with <a href="/wiki/Hasely_Crawford_Stadium" title="Hasely Crawford Stadium">Hasely Crawford Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain, Trinidad</a> are the venues for the women's competition.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Group_stage">Group stage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2010_FIFA_U-17_Women%27s_World_Cup&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Group stage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The opening phase of the tournament comprised four groups of four teams, with the top two sides in each section advancing to the quarter-finals. The final draw to determine the groups took place in <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> on May 5, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>Tie breakers in the group stage are:</p>
<ol>
<li>greatest number of points obtained in all group matches</li>
<li>goal difference in all group matches</li>
<li>greatest number of goals scored in all group matches</li>
</ol>
<p>If more than two or more teams are still tied after that:</p>
<ol>
<li>greatest number of points obtained in matches between concerned teams</li>
<li>goal difference in matches between concerned teams</li>
<li>greatest number of goals scored in matches between concerned teams</li>
<li>fair play point system, in which the yellow and red cards of group matches are evaluated</li>
<li>drawing of lots</li>
</ol>
